 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center"><B><A NAME="toc832592_1"></A>PART I </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center"><B>INTRODUCTION </B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:9%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Unless
otherwise indicated, all references herein to &#147;Ericsson,&#148; the &#147;Company,&#148; &#147;the Group,&#148; &#147;we,&#148; &#147;us,&#148; or &#147;our&#148; or &#147;our company&#148; are references to Telefonaktiebolaget LM Ericsson and
its consolidated subsidiaries. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:9%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">This document is our Annual Report on Form <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">20-F</FONT> for the year ended
December&nbsp;31, 2019 (the &#147;2019 Form <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">20-F&#148;).</FONT> Reference is made to the English version of our Swedish Annual Report for 2019, with certain adjustments made to comply with U.S. requirements, which is
attached hereto as Exhibit 15.1 (the &#147;2019 Swedish Annual Report&#148;). Only (i)&nbsp;the information included in this 2019 Form <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">20-F,</FONT> (ii)&nbsp;the information in the 2019 Swedish Annual Report that is
incorporated by reference in this 2019 Form <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">20-F,</FONT> and (iii)&nbsp;the exhibits to the 2019 Form <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">20-F</FONT> that are required to be filed pursuant to the Form <FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">20-F</FONT> shall be deemed to be filed with the Securities and Exchange Commission for any purpose, including incorporation by reference into the Registration Statement on Form <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">F-3</FONT>
filed on March&nbsp;27, 2018 (File <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">No.&nbsp;333-223954)</FONT> and any other document filed by us pursuant to the Securities Act of 1933, as amended, which incorporates by reference the 2019 Form <FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">20-F.</FONT> Any information in the 2019 Swedish Annual Report that is not referenced in the 2019 Form <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">20-F</FONT> or filed as an exhibit thereto shall not be deemed to be so incorporated
by reference. Certain industry, technical and financial terms used in this 2019 Form <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">20-F</FONT> are defined in the subsections entitled &#147;Glossary&#148; and &#147;Financial Terminology&#148; of the 2019 Swedish
Annual Report, which are incorporated herein by reference. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:9%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Market data and certain industry forecasts used herein were obtained from
internal surveys, market research, publicly available information and industry publications. While we believe that market research, publicly available information and industry publications we use are reliable, we have not independently verified
market and industry data from third-party sources. Moreover, while we believe our internal surveys are reliable, they have not been verified by any independent source. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:9%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The information included on <U>http://www.ericsson.com/</U> and other websites that appear in this 2019 Form
<FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">20-F</FONT> is not incorporated by reference herein. From time to time, we may use our website as a channel of distribution of material company information. Financial and other material information regarding our
company is routinely posted on and accessible at <U>http://www.ericsson.com/</U>. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Forward-Looking Statements </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:9%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">This 2019 Form <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">20-F</FONT> includes forward-looking statements, including statements reflecting
management&#146;s current views relating to the growth of the market, future market conditions, future events, financial condition, and expected operational and financial performance, including, in particular the following: </P>
<P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>

<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>General facts on the company </I></B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Legal and
commercial name of the Parent Company: </B>Telefonaktiebolaget LM Ericsson (publ). </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Organization number: </B>556016-0680 </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Legal form of the Parent Company: </B>A Swedish limited liability company, organized under the Swedish Companies Act. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Country of incorporation: </B>Sweden. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Date of
incorporation: </B>The Parent Company was incorporated on August&nbsp;18, 1918, as a result of a merger between AB LM Ericsson&nbsp;&amp; Co. and Stockholms Allm&auml;nna Telefon AB. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Domicile: </B>Our registered office is Telefonaktiebolaget LM Ericsson, SE&#150;164 83 Stockholm, Sweden. Our headquarters are located at Torshamnsgatan
21, Kista, Sweden. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Telephone number: </B>+46 10 719 0000 </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Website: </B><U>www.ericsson.com</U>. The information included on our website is not incorporated herein by reference. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">In addition, the SEC maintains an Internet site that contains reports, proxy and information statements, and other information regarding issuers that file
electronically with the SEC: <U>http://www.sec.gov</U>. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Agent in the US: </B>Ericsson Inc., Vice President Legal Affairs, 6300 Legacy Drive, Plano,
Texas 75024. Telephone number: +1 972 583 0000. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Shares: </B>Ericsson&#146;s Class&nbsp;A and Class&nbsp;B shares are traded on Nasdaq Stockholm. In
the US, our American Depository Shares (ADS), each representing one underlying Class&nbsp;B share, are traded on NASDAQ New York. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Parent company
operations: </B>The business of the parent company, Telefonaktiebolaget LM Ericsson, consists mainly of corporate management, holding company functions and internal banking activities. Our parent company operations also include customer credit
management activities performed by Ericsson Credit AB on a commission basis. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Subsidiaries and associated companies: </B>For a list of our significant
subsidiaries, please see &#147;Item 4C. Shares owned directly by the Parent Company &#148;. We are engaged in a number of minor joint ventures and cooperative arrangements. For more information regarding risks associated with joint ventures,
strategic alliances and third-party agreements, please see &#147;Item 3D. Financials&#150;Risk Factors&#151;Market, Technology and Business Risks&#148;. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Company history and development </I></B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><U>Innovating to
empower people, business and society </U></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Our origins date back to 1876 when Alexander Graham Bell filed a patent application in the United
States for the telephone. The same year, Lars Magnus Ericsson opened a small workshop in Stockholm to repair telegraph instruments and sell his own telephone equipment. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Today, Ericsson enables communications service providers to capture the full value of connectivity. The company&#146;s portfolio spans
Networks, Digital Services, Managed Services, and Emerging Business and is designed to help our customers go digital, increase efficiency and find new revenue streams. Ericsson&#146;s investments in innovation have delivered the benefits of
telephony and mobile broadband to billions of people around the world. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:9%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The information set forth under the following headings of the 2019
Swedish Annual Report is incorporated herein by reference: </P> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>

<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="19%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="2%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt">Significant topics, risks and opportunities </P></TD></TR></TABLE>
<P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="19%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="2%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt">Responsible business &#150; Responsible management of suppliers </P></TD></TR></TABLE>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Disclosure pursuant to Section&nbsp;219 of the Iran Threat Reduction and Syria Human Rights Act of 2012 (ITRA) </I></B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Ericsson has conducted business in Iran/Persia since the late nineteenth century, opened an office in Iran in 1973 and later established a local subsidiary in
the country. Ericsson strongly believes in enabling communication for all and believes that access to communications can enable the right to health, education and freedom of expression. Ericsson&#146;s business activities in Iran principally involve
the sale of communications infrastructure related products and services, including support, installation and maintenance services. Ericsson&#146;s exports from the European Union (the &#147;EU&#148;) to Iran are performed under export licenses from
the Swedish Inspectorate of Strategic Products and in compliance with applicable economic sanctions and export controls. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Due to its operations in Iran,
and having staff permanently in the country, Ericsson has contacts with its local customers and retains certain local suppliers, including banks, and service providers. In addition, Ericsson has other dealings incidental to its local activities,
such as making payments for taxes, salaries, rents, utilities and office and similar supplies as well for local accommodation and transportation and customs related services. As a result, Ericsson has contact with companies and public functions that
may be owned or controlled by the government of Iran. While Ericsson seeks to obtain information regarding the actual business names and ownership of customers and other counterparties in Iran through its policies and procedures designed to ensure
that Ericsson &#147;knows its customers&#148;, it is challenging to determine ownership and control with certainty, particularly with respect to determining whether an entity engaged in commercial activities is owned or controlled by the government.
</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">During 2019, Ericsson sold communications infrastructure related products and services in Iran to the following telecommunications companies operating in
the country: Mobile Communication Company of Iran (&#147;MCCI&#148;), and MTN Irancell. During 2019, Ericsson&#146;s gross revenue (reported as net sales) related to sales to MCCI and MTN Irancell in Iran was approximately SEK 908&nbsp;million. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Ericsson does not normally allocate net profit (reported as net income) on a
<FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">country-by-country</FONT></FONT> or <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">activity-by-activity</FONT></FONT> basis, other than as set forth in
Ericsson&#146;s consolidated financial statements prepared in accordance with IFRS as issued by the IASB. However, Ericsson has estimated that its operating income (income before taxes and financial net) from such sales was, after internal cost
allocation approximately SEK 95&nbsp;million during 2019. Ericsson always strives to honor its engagements with existing customers in compliance with applicable export controls, sanctions and other laws, rules and regulations, but it is clear that
the extensive U.S. sanctions impact the overall possibility of doing business in Iran. Ericsson carefully evaluates the implications of any sanctions and continues to monitor developments in this area as it relates to the ability to continue
delivering products and services to customers. Ericsson has reduced its business and organization in Iran but still continues to fulfill engagements with the two main mobile carriers, MCCI and MTN Irancell and to provide them with what is critical
for their networks to function. As Ericsson provides these services, it may need to interact with other counterparties. Ericsson continues to explore, including with EU and US authorities, whether and how the disruptive impact on the ability to
maintain and support the operations of existing networks of MCCI and MTN Irancell can be reduced and, by doing so, endeavor to avoid undue impacts on the access of the people of Iran to humanitarian items/basic services such as telecommunications.
</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">In some instances, Ericsson has had to arrange performance bonds or similar financial guarantees to secure Ericsson&#146;s performance of obligations
under the commercial agreements Ericsson has entered into relating to the business in Iran. In such instances, Ericsson usually engages its banks outside Iran, who in turn engage local banks in the country. These local banks include Tejarat Bank,
Melli Bank, Parsian Bank and Saderat Bank. Although some bonds and guarantees are still in place, no new performance bonds or similar guarantees involving these four banks with respect to Ericsson&#146;s business activities in Iran were issued
during 2019. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">During 2019, existing bank guarantees issued by Maskan Bank, Parsian Bank, Post Bank of Iran and Tejarat Bank (local banks in Iran) to
secure Iranian customer payment obligations to Ericsson were renewed. Further, some payments made to Ericsson&#146;s local subsidiary and payments required to be made by the local subsidiary to suppliers involve banks that may be controlled by the
government of Iran. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><A NAME="toc832592_12"></A><A NAME="toc832592_12"></A>C. Organizational Structure </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:9%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The following list shows certain shareholdings owned directly and indirectly by our parent company as of December&nbsp;31, 2019. A complete
list of shareholdings, prepared in accordance with the Swedish Annual Accounts Act and filed with the Swedish Companies Registration Office (Bolagsverket), may be obtained upon request to: Telefonaktiebolaget LM Ericsson, External Reporting, <FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">SE-164</FONT> 83 Stockholm, Sweden. </P>
 <p STYLE="margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt ; font-size:8pt">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center">4 </P>

<TD WIDTH="4%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">**</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman; " ALIGN="left">Test capacity utilization. </P></TD></TR></TABLE>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:9%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">In June 2019, the Company announced plans to build its first fully-automated smart factory in the US. The 300,000 square-foot smart factory
will begin commercial operations in March 2020, in Lewisville, TX. The <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">state-of-the-art</FONT></FONT></FONT> factory will produce 5G and Advanced
Antenna System radios to boost network capacity and coverage to meet the demand for rapid 5G deployments in North America. The company&#146;s direct investment in the factory is approximately USD $100&nbsp;million. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:9%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">In September 2019, the Company announced that its 269,000 square-foot factory in Tallinn, Estonia, was nearing completion of its <FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">two-year</FONT> digitalization transformation, in the amount of SEK 500&nbsp;million, to become a 5G manufacturing facility utilizing Ericsson&#146;s own 5G technology. The factory will be fully operational during the
first quarter of 2020. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:9%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">In September 2019, the company announced it concluded the <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">18-month</FONT>
upgrade, in the amount of SEK 500&nbsp;million, to modernize the production process (of 5G and 4G radio technology products) in its smart factory in Nanjing, China, in preparation for the introduction and rapid deployments of 5G in China. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:9%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The investments are financed by cash flow from operations or by the financing activities described in our Swedish Annual Report 2019. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:9%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The information set forth under the following headings of the 2019 Swedish Annual Report is incorporated herein by reference: </P>

<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt">Note A1 &#150; Significant accounting policies </P></TD></TR></TABLE>
<P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="27%">&nbsp;</TD>

<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt">Note F1 &#150; Financial risk management&#150; Foreign exchange risk </P></TD></TR></TABLE>
<P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="19%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="2%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt">Risk Factors </P></TD></TR></TABLE>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I><U>Operating results for the years ended December</U><U></U><U>&nbsp;31, 2017 and 2018</U> </I></B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Financial highlights </B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Net sales </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Sales increased by SEK&nbsp;5.5&nbsp;billion or 3% to SEK&nbsp;210.8 (205.4) billion. Networks sales increased by SEK&nbsp;6.3&nbsp;billion (5%), Digital
Services sales decreased by SEK&nbsp;&#150;0.7&nbsp;billion (&#150;2%), Managed Services sales decreased by SEK&nbsp;&#150;0.7&nbsp;billion (&#150;3%) and Emerging Business and Other sales increased by SEK&nbsp;0.5&nbsp;billion (7%). </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The sales increase in Networks was mainly driven by higher demand for radio access network equipment. Networks sales growth adjusted for comparable units and
currency was 3%. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The sales decrease in segment Digital Services was due to lower sales in legacy products. The sales decline in Managed Services was
mainly a result of exit of <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">low-performing</FONT> and <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-strategic</FONT> contracts. The sales increase in segment Emerging Business and Other was driven by growth in iconectiv
business due to the multi-year number portability contract in the United States. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">In the geographical dimension, sales grew in North America and in Europe
and Latin America. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Sales adjusted for comparable units and currency increased by 1%. The sales mix by commodity was: software 21% (21%), hardware 37%
(35%) and services 42% (44%). </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Gross margin </B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Gross
margin increased to 32.3% (23.3%) with improved margins in hardware and services mainly driven by cost reductions, <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">ramp-up</FONT> of Ericsson Radio System product platform and good progress in the review of <FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">low-performing</FONT> managed services contracts. A reduced share of services sales had a positive impact on gross margin. Restructuring charges included in the gross margin increased to SEK&nbsp;&#150;5.9 (&#150;5.2)
billion. Costs of SEK&nbsp;&#150;5.9&nbsp;billion, of which SEK&nbsp;&#150;3.1&nbsp;billion were restructuring charges, impacted gross margin in Digital Services. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Due to technology and portfolio shifts, the company has since 2017 reduced the capitalization of development expenses and the deferral of hardware costs,
which had a net impact on gross income of SEK&nbsp;&#150;0.9 (&#150;2.6) billion. Write-down of assets, as well as provisions and adjustments related to certain customer projects had a significant negative impact on gross margin in 2017. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Operating expenses </B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Operating expenses decreased to
SEK&nbsp;&#150;66.8 (&#150;70.6) billion with SG&amp;A expenses of SEK&nbsp;&#150;27.5 (&#150;29.0) billion, R&amp;D expenses of SEK&nbsp;&#150;38.9 (&#150;37.9) billion and impairment losses on trade receivables of SEK&nbsp;&#150;0.4 (&#150;3.6)
billion. Restructuring charges included in operating expenses were SEK&nbsp;&#150;2.1 (&#150;3.3) billion. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">R&amp;D expenses increased due to increased
investments in R&amp;D for Networks. The increase was partly offset by R&amp;D reductions in Digital Services. Higher amortized than capitalized development expenses had a negative effect on R&amp;D expenses of SEK&nbsp;&#150;1.7 (&#150;0.3)
billion. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">SG&amp;A expenses were reduced as a result of cost reduction activities. The reduction was more than offset by higher provisions for variable
compensation, increased costs related to revaluation of customer financing and increased costs for 5G trials. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Other operating income and expenses
</B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Other operating income and expenses was SEK&nbsp;&#150;0.2 (&#150;12.1) billion. In 2017, write-down of intangible assets had a significant negative
impact on other operating expenses. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt;page-break-before:always"></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Consequences of technology and portfolio
shifts </B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Due to technology and portfolio shifts the company is reducing the capitalization of development expenses for product platforms and software
releases and the deferral of hardware costs. As a consequence, higher amortization than capitalization of development expenses and higher recognition than deferral of hardware costs had a negative impact on operating income of SEK&nbsp;&#150;2.6
(&#150;2.9) billion. The amounts related to capitalized software releases were fully amortized in&nbsp;2017. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Restructuring charges </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Restructuring charges amounted to SEK&nbsp;&#150;8.0 (&#150;8.5) billion, which was higher than the earlier estimate of SEK&nbsp;&#150;5 to
&#150;7&nbsp;billion. The restructuring charges in 2018 mainly relate to the cost-reduction program announced in 2017 and costs related to revised BSS strategy. Total restructuring charges for 2019 are estimated to be SEK&nbsp;&#150;3 to
&#150;5&nbsp;billion. </P>
 <p STYLE="margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt ; font-size:8pt">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center">7 </P>

</DIV></Center>

hardware costs </B></P> <P STYLE="font-size:12pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>

<TR BGCOLOR="#cceeff" STYLE="page-break-inside:avoid ; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt">
<TD VALIGN="top"> <P STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; margin-left:1.00em; text-indent:-1.00em; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Cost of sales</P></TD>

<TD NOWRAP VALIGN="bottom">&nbsp;</TD></TR>
</TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Operating income and margin </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Operating income improved to SEK&nbsp;1.2 (&#150;34.7) billion. Higher gross margin and sales and lower operating expenses had a positive impact. Write-down of
assets, as well as provisions and adjustments related to certain customer projects had a significant negative impact on operating income in 2017. Operating margin was 0.6% (&#150;16.9%). Operating margin excluding restructuring charges of
SEK&nbsp;&#150;8.0 (&#150;8.5) billion was 4.4% (&#150;12.8%). </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Financial net </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The financial net decreased to SEK&nbsp;&#150;2.7 (&#150;1.2) billion, mainly due to increased negative effects of foreign exchange revaluation, negative
currency hedge effects and reduced interest rates. The currency hedge effects, which derive from the hedge loan balance in USD, impacted financial net by SEK&nbsp;&#150;0.5 (0.5) billion. The SEK weakened against the USD between December&nbsp;31,
2017 (SEK/USD rate 8.20) and December&nbsp;31, 2018 (SEK/USD rate&nbsp;8.94). </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Taxes </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Taxes were SEK&nbsp;&#150;4.8 (3.5) billion, negatively impacted by impairment of withholding tax assets in Sweden mainly as a result of <FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">pro-visions</FONT> related to revised BSS strategy. In addition, <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-deductible</FONT> expenses, with-holding tax expenses outside of Sweden and&nbsp;revaluation of tax assets due to a
change in Swedish corporate tax rate impacted tax costs negatively. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Net income and EPS </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Net income improved to SEK&nbsp;&#150;6.3 (&#150;32.4) billion driven by higher operating income partly offset by a negative financial net and increased tax
costs. EPS diluted was SEK&nbsp;&#150;1.98 (&#150;9.94) and EPS <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">(non-IFRS)</FONT> was SEK&nbsp;0.27 (&#150;3.24). </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Employees </B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The number of employees on December&nbsp;31,
2018 was 95,359, a reduction of 5,376 employees compared with Dec 31, 2017. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The employee reduction was mainly in services as a consequence of the
cost-reduction program. The number of R&amp;D employees has increased by more than 1,100 in 2018. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Business results &#150; Segments </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Networks </B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Networks represented 66% (64%) of net sales in
2018. The segment delivers products and services that are needed for mobile and fixed communication, several generations of radio networks and transmission networks. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Net sales </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Sales increased by 5% to SEK&nbsp;138.6 (132.3)
billion. Sales adjusted for comparable units and currency increased by 3%. The sales increase was due to sales growth in North America and in Europe and Latin America, driven by telecom operator investments in 5G readiness and LTE networks. The
Networks share of IPR licensing revenues was SEK&nbsp;6.5 (6.8) billion. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Gross margin </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Gross income increased to SEK&nbsp;55.2 (43.4) billion and gross margin increased to 39.8% (32.8%). Gross margin increased across all areas, mainly due to
improved margins in hardware and a higher share of hardware sales at the expense of services sales. The impact on gross margin of higher recognition than deferral of hardware costs was SEK&nbsp;&#150;0.7 (&#150;1.5) billion. In 2017 the gross margin
was negatively impacted by provisions and customer project adjustments. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Operating income </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Operating income increased to SEK&nbsp;19.4 (10.5) billion due to lower restructuring charges as well as higher sales and gross margin. The increase was partly
offset by increased operating expenses. Operating expenses increased mainly due to higher investments in R&amp;D to strengthened tech-nology leadership. Net impact from amortization and capitalization of development expenses and from recognition and
deferral of&nbsp;hardware costs was SEK&nbsp;&#150;0.3 (&#150;1.5) billion. Restructuring charges were SEK&nbsp;&#150;1.8 (&#150;4.8) billion. Operating margin increased to&nbsp;14.0%&nbsp;(7.9%). </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Digital Services </B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Digital Services represented 18% (19%)
of net sales in 2018. The segment provides solutions consisting primarily of software and services in the areas of Digital Business Support Systems (BSS), Operational Support Systems (OSS), Cloud Communication, Cloud Core, and Cloud Infrastructure.
</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Net sales </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Sales decreased by &#150;2%. Sales in BSS
declined by &#150;11% while sales in OSS and Cloud Core grew, driven by demand for the <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">5G-ready</FONT> portfolio. Sales adjusted for comparable units and currency decreased by &#150;4%. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Gross margin </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Gross margin increased to 21.8% (12.1%) as a
result of cont-inuous work on service delivery efficiency. Gross margin was negatively impacted by costs related to revised BSS strategy, while cost reductions had a significant positive impact. Gross margin was negatively impacted by significant
write-down of assets as well as provisions and customer project adjustments in 2017. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Operating income (loss) </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Operating income improved to SEK&nbsp;&#150;13.9 (&#150;27.3) billion. Full-year operating income was SEK&nbsp;&#150;5.5&nbsp;billion, excluding restructuring
charges of SEK&nbsp;&#150;5.4&nbsp;billion and excluding SEK&nbsp;&#150;3.0&nbsp;billion for other costs related to revised BSS strategy. This is a significant improvement compared with 2017, with profit improvements across all key portfolio areas.
Most of the losses in 2018 are in BSS, and additional strategic actions to materially reduce the losses already in&nbsp;2019 were announced in January 2019. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Write-down of assets as well as provisions and customer project adjustments had a significant negative impact on income in 2017. Cost reductions had a
significant impact on gross margin and operating expenses compared with&nbsp;2017. </P>
 <p STYLE="margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt ; font-size:8pt">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center">8 </P>

</DIV></Center>


<p style="margin-top:1em; margin-bottom:0em; page-break-before:always">
<HR SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">
<h5 align="left"><a href="#toc">Table of Contents</a></h5>


<Center><DIV STYLE="width:8.5in" align="left">
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Managed Services </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Managed Services represented 12% (13%) of&nbsp;net sales in 2018. The segment delivers managed services and network optimization to telecom operators. Through
these offerings, customers entrust Ericsson to run the operations of their network/IT systems and optimize network performance. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Net sales </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Sales decreased by &#150;3%. Sales adjusted for comparable units and currency decreased by &#150;5%, as a result of contract exits, partly offset by sales
growth in Managed Services IT. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Gross margin </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Gross margin
increased to 11.2% (&#150;5.9%) mainly as a result of customer contract reviews and efficiency measures. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Write-down of assets as well as provisions and
customer project adjustments had a significant negative impact on gross margin in 2017. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Operating income </B> </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Operating income improved to SEK&nbsp;1.1 (&#150;4.1) billion due to higher gross margin. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Restructuring charges amounted to SEK&nbsp;&#150;0.3 (&#150;0.7) billion. <B> </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Emerging Business and Other</B> </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Segment Emerging Business
and Other represented 4% (4%) of net sales in 2018. The&nbsp;segment consists of four businesses; Media Solutions, Red Bee Media, Emerging Business and iconectiv. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Net sales </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Sales increased by 7%. Sales adjusted for comparable
units and currency increased by 3%, driven by growth in the iconectiv business through a multi-year number portability contract in the United States. Sales in Emerging Business grew by more than 25%. Media Solutions sales declined by &#150;14% due
to lower sales in the legacy portfolio. Red Bee Media sales declined by &#150;4% due to renegotiations and changes in scope of contracts. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Gross margin
</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Gross margin increased to 21.9% (17.5%). Write-down of assets had a significant negative impact on gross margin in 2017. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Operating income (loss) </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Operating income (loss) improved to SEK
&#150;5.4 (&#150;13.8) billion with significant improvements in Media Solutions and Red Bee Media business. Restructuring charges amounted to&nbsp;SEK&nbsp;&#150;0.6 (&#150;0.5) billion. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Cost reductions had a positive impact on Media Solutions operating income, partly offset by reduced sales and costs of SEK&nbsp;&#150;0.3&nbsp;billion related
to the transaction with One Equity Partners. Write-down of assets had a significant negative impact on Media Solutions income in 2017. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Operational
efficiencies and cost reductions had a positive impact on Red Bee Media income, while reduced sales impacted negatively. Write-down of assets had a significant negative impact on Red Bee Media income in 2017. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Losses in Emerging Business were negatively impacted by costs of SEK&nbsp;&#150;0.4&nbsp;billion, of which SEK&nbsp;&#150;0.1&nbsp;billion in restructuring
charges, for resetting the Edge Gravity business and increased investments in new areas such as IoT and Emodo. The growth in iconectiv business had a positive impact on operating income. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Business results &#150; Market areas </B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>South East Asia,
Oceania and India </B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Sales declined, mainly due to timing of major projects in Vietnam and India. Managed services sales grew slightly mainly due to a
new contract, while sales in Digital Services remained flat. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>North East Asia </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Sales declined due to reduced operator investments in LTE whilst the operators plan for 5G. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>North America </B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Networks sales increased, primarily driven
by investments in 5G readiness across all major customers. Digital Services sales increased as operators digitalize operations and improve customer experience to prepare for 5G. Managed Services sales grew, driven by higher variable sales in large
customer contracts. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Europe and Latin America </B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The
strong growth in Networks sales in Latin America and parts of Europe was partly offset by lower sales in Managed Services due to exit of <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-strategic</FONT> contracts. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Middle East and Africa </B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Sales declined slightly. Networks
sales declined due to monetary restrictions in certain markets, Digital Services declined due to timing of project milestones while Managed Services sales were flat. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Other<SUP STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">1)</SUP> </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Sales declined slightly. IPR licensing revenues amounted to SEK&nbsp;8.0 (8.3) billion. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt;page-break-before:always"></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Sales per market area and segment 2018 and percent change from 2017 </B></P>

<Center><DIV STYLE="width:8.5in" align="left">

<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt">Note H3 &#150; Statement of cash flows </P></TD></TR></TABLE>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; margin-left:9%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">See &#147;Item 8.B. Financial Information &#150; Significant Changes&#148; herein. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I><U>Balance sheet and other performance indicators for the years ended December&nbsp;31, 2017 and 2018 </U></I></B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Cash flow </B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Cash flow from operating activities reached
SEK&nbsp;9.3 (9.6) billion. Working capital efficiency has improved as a result of a strong focus on cash flow. The business growth in 2018 and high delivery and invoicing volumes towards the end of the year led to some <FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">build-up</FONT> of trade receivables, to be collected in the coming periods. Inventory and trade payables also increased to meet customer demand in a growing market. The combined working capital KPI (sales outstanding days
plus inventory days less payable days) improved to 89 (102) days. The ambition is to maintain working capital efficiency and thereby effectively convert income to cash. Cash outlays related to provisions were SEK&nbsp;&#150;6.9 (&#150;8.2) billion,
of which cash outlays related to restructuring charges were SEK&nbsp;&#150;4.1 (&#150;5.3) billion. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Cash flow from investing activities was
SEK&nbsp;&#150;4.1 (&#150;16.1) billion, impacted by investments and sale of property, plant and equipment with a net effect of SEK&nbsp;&#150;3.6 (&#150;2.9) billion and investments in M&amp;A of SEK&nbsp;&#150;1.3 (0.3) billion. In addition,
product development decreased by SEK&nbsp;&#150;0.9 (&#150;1.4) billion due to reduced capitalization of product platform development following technology shifts. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Cash flow from financing activities was SEK&nbsp;&#150;4.1 (5.5) billion. Dividends of SEK&nbsp;3.4 (3.4) billion were paid out. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The focus on free cash flow and release of working capital, in combination with limited investing activities, resulted in free cash flow of SEK&nbsp;3.0 (5.1)
billion and in free cash flow excluding M&amp;A of SEK&nbsp;4.3 (4.8) billion. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Financial position </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Gross cash increased to SEK&nbsp;69.0 (67.7) billion and net cash increased to SEK&nbsp;35.9 (34.7) billion. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Liability for post-employments benefits increased by SEK&nbsp;3.7&nbsp;billion mainly due to decreased discount rates and normal service costs. The Swedish
defined benefit obligation (DBO) has been calculated using a discount rate based on the yields of Swedish government bonds. If the discount rate had been based on Swedish covered mortgage bonds, the liability for post-employment benefits would have
been approximately SEK&nbsp;9.5&nbsp;billion lower as of Dec 31, 2018. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The average maturity of long-term borrowings as of Dec 31, 2018, was 3.4 years, a
decrease from 4.4 years 12 months earlier. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Ericsson has an unutilized Revolving Credit Facility of USD 2.0&nbsp;billion. The facility will expire in
2022. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">In 2018, Ericsson signed a credit facility agreement of EUR 250&nbsp;million with the European Investment Bank (EIB). The credit<I> </I>facility is
undrawn and will mature five years after disbursement. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Moody&#146;s changed their outlook on Ericsson&#146;s long-term rating from negative
to&nbsp;stable. The rating of Ba2 was unchanged. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The capital efficiency improved during the year and the capital turnover reached 1.4 (1.2)&nbsp;times.
</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Research and development, -patents&nbsp;and&nbsp;licensing </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">In 2018, R&amp;D expenses amounted to&nbsp;SEK&nbsp;38.9 (37.9) billion. The increase is mainly due to investments in Networks R&amp;D to increase the
competitiveness and profitability of the radio product portfolio. The number of R&amp;D resources were 24,800. The number of patents continued to increase and amounted to approximately 49,000 by end of 2018. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Research and development, patents and licensing </B></P> <P STYLE="font-size:12pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>

<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Seasonality </B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The Company&#146;s sales, income and cash
flow from operations vary between quarters, and are generally lowest in the first quarter of the year and highest in the fourth quarter. This is mainly a result of the seasonal purchase-patterns of network operators. </P>

</TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">Off-balance</FONT> sheet arrangements </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">There are currently no material <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">off-balance</FONT> sheet arrangements that have, or would be reasonably likely to have, a
current or anticipated material effect on the Company&#146;s financial condition, revenues, expenses, result of operations, liquidity, capital expenditures or&nbsp;capital resources. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Capital expenditures </B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">For 2018, capital expenditure was
SEK&nbsp;4.0 (3.9) billion, representing 1.9% of sales. Expenditures are largely related to test sites and equipment for R&amp;D, network operation centers and manufacturing and repair operations. </P>
 <p STYLE="margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt ; font-size:8pt">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center">10 </P>

</DIV></Center>


<p style="margin-top:1em; margin-bottom:0em; page-break-before:always">
<HR SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">
<h5 align="left"><a href="#toc">Table of Contents</a></h5>


<Center><DIV STYLE="width:8.5in" align="left">
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Ericsson believes that the Company&#146;s property, plant and&nbsp;equipment and the fac-ilities the Company
occupies are suitable for its&nbsp;present needs. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Annual capital expenditures are normally around 2% of sales. This corresponds to the needs for keeping
and maintaining the current capacity level. The Board of Directors reviews the Company&#146;s investment plans and proposals. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">As of December&nbsp;31,
2018, no material land, buildings, machinery or equipment were pledged as collateral for outstanding indebtedness. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Capital expenditures 2016&#150;2018

<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><A NAME="toc832592_34"></A>B. Significant Changes </B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>US
Securities class action </B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On January&nbsp;11, 2020, the United States District Court for the Southern District of New York granted Ericsson&#146;s
motion to dismiss the putative class action filed in 2018 against Telefonaktiebolaget LM Ericsson, the present President and CEO and the Chief Financial Officer of Ericsson as well as three former executives. At the same time the court granted
plaintiffs leave to file a third amended complaint within thirty days. The plaintiffs did not file an amended complaint by the court-ordered deadline. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Sol IP Settlement </B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Ericsson has after the <FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">year-end</FONT> 2019 resolved the previously communicated litigation with Sol IP, concerning alleged infringement of 20 patents declared to the LTE standard. The patents originated from Electronics and Telecommunications
Research Institute (ETRI), a Korean government-funded research institution. The settlement resolves the litigation with Sol IP and involves a patent license agreement between Ericsson, Sol IP and ETRI. The settlement will have a negative impact for
2020 of approximately USD 13&nbsp;million on operating income within Segment Networks of which USD 10&nbsp;million will be recorded in Q1 2020 and the balance spread equally over the remaining quarters. This quarterly license fee amortization will
continue in subsequent periods. The exact terms of the agreement are confidential. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Ericsson to acquire Genaker to strengthen Mission Critical <FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">Push-to-talk</FONT></FONT> offering </B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On March&nbsp;12, 2020, Ericsson announced that it had
signed an agreement to acquire 100&nbsp;percent of the shares in Genaker, a provider of Mission Critical <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">Push-to-talk</FONT></FONT> <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">(MC-PTT)</FONT>
solutions. The acquisition strengthens Ericsson&#146;s <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">MC-PTT</FONT> offering as the mission critical communications and private network market is going through a significant technology shift. Genaker, located in
Barcelona, Spain, was founded in 2004 and employs around 30 people, all of whom will transfer to Ericsson as part of the acquisition. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Pandemics, such
as for example the one caused by the Coronavirus, COVID-19, could severely impact our local and global operations </B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Pandemics, such as for example the
one caused by the Coronavirus, could severely impact our local and global operations related to e.g. Service Delivery, Research &amp; Development, Sales and Supply, as well as our customers and suppliers, with significant financial and other
consequences. As an example, the Coronavirus has caused disturbance to our operations in China where Ericsson has offices and manufacturing sites. It is starting to cause similar disruptions to Ericsson&#146;s operations and those of its customers
and suppliers in other countries and to negatively impact the global economy. The effects of those disruptions may have material adverse effects on our business and financial position. </P>

<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><A NAME="toc832592_46"></A>D. Exchange Controls </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:9%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">There is no Swedish legislation affecting the import or export of capital or the remittance of dividends, interest or other payments to <FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-resident</FONT> holders of our securities, except that, subject to the provisions in any tax treaty, dividends are subject to withholding tax. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><A NAME="toc832592_47"></A>E. Taxation </B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>General
</I></B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:9%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The taxation discussion set forth below does not purport to be a complete analysis or listing of all potential tax effects
relevant to the acquisition, ownership or disposition of Class&nbsp;B shares or ADSs. The statements of United States and Swedish tax laws set forth below are based on the laws in force as of the date of this report and may be subject to any changes
in United States or Swedish law, and in any double taxation convention or treaty between the United States and Sweden, occurring after that date, which changes may then have retroactive effect. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:9%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Specific tax provisions may apply for certain categories of taxpayers. Your tax treatment if you are a holder of Class&nbsp;B shares or ADSs
depends in part on your particular situation. If you are a holder of Class&nbsp;B shares or ADSs, you should therefore consult a tax advisor as to the tax consequences relating to your particular circumstances resulting from the ownership of
Class&nbsp;B shares or ADSs. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:9%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The tax consequences to holders of ADSs, as discussed below, apply equally to holders of Class&nbsp;B
shares. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Certain Swedish Tax Considerations </I></B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:9%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">This section describes the material Swedish income and net wealth tax consequences for a holder of ADSs or Class&nbsp;B shares who is not
considered to be a Swedish resident for Swedish tax purposes. This section applies to you only if you are a holder of portfolio investments representing less than 10% of capital and votes and is not applicable if the ADSs or Class&nbsp;B shares
pertain to a permanent establishment or fixed place of business in Sweden. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><U>Taxation on Capital Gains </U></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:9%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Generally, <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-residents</FONT> of Sweden are not liable for Swedish capital gains taxation with respect to
the sale of ADSs or Class&nbsp;B shares. However, under Swedish tax law, capital gains from the sale of shares in Swedish companies and certain other securities by an individual may be taxed in Sweden at a rate of 30% if the seller has been a
resident of Sweden or has lived permanently in Sweden at any time during the year of the sale or the 10 calendar years preceding the year of the sale (absent treaty provisions to the contrary). The provision is applicable to ADSs or Class&nbsp;B
shares. From January&nbsp;1, 2008, the rule has been extended so that it also applies to shares in foreign companies, provided that the shares were acquired during the time that the person was liable to tax in Sweden. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:9%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">This provision may, however, be limited by tax treaties that Sweden has concluded with other countries. Under the tax treaty between Sweden
and the United States (the &#147;U.S. Tax Treaty&#148;), this provision applies for ten years from the date the individual became a <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-resident</FONT> of Sweden. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><U>Taxation on Dividends </U></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:9%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">A Swedish dividend
withholding tax at a rate of 30% is imposed on dividends paid by a Swedish corporation, such as us, to <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-residents</FONT> of Sweden. The same withholding tax applies to certain other payments made by a Swedish
corporation, including payments as a result of redemption of shares and repurchase of stock through an offer directed to its shareholders. Exemption from the withholding tax or a lower tax rate may apply by virtue of a tax treaty. Under the U.S. Tax
Treaty, the withholding tax on dividends paid on portfolio investments to eligible U.S. holders is reduced to 15%. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:9%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Under all Swedish tax
treaties, except the tax treaty with Switzerland, withholding tax at the applicable treaty rate should be withheld by the payer of the dividends. With regard to dividends paid from shares in corporations registered with the Euroclear Sweden (such as
our shares), a reduced rate of dividend withholding tax under a tax treaty is generally applied at the source by the Euroclear Sweden or, if the shares are registered with a nominee, the nominee, as long as the person entitled to the dividend is
registered as a <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-resident</FONT> and sufficient information regarding the tax residency of the beneficial owner is available to the Euroclear Sweden or the nominee. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:9%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">In those cases where Swedish withholding tax is withheld at the rate of 30% and the person who received the dividends is entitled to a reduced
rate of withholding tax under a tax treaty, a refund may be claimed from the Swedish tax authorities before the end of the fifth calendar year following the year that the distribution was made. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><U>Taxation on Interest </U></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:9%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">No Swedish
withholding tax is payable on interest paid to <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-residents</FONT> of Sweden. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><U>Net Wealth Taxation </U></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:9%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The Swedish net wealth tax has been abolished from January&nbsp;1, 2007. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Certain United States Federal Income Tax Consequences </I></B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:9%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The following discussion is a summary of the material United States federal income tax consequences relevant to the ownership and disposition
of ADSs or Class&nbsp;B shares. This discussion is based on the tax laws of the United States (including the Internal Revenue Code of 1986, as amended (the &#147;Code&#148;), its legislative history, existing and proposed regulations thereunder,
published rulings and court decisions) as in effect on the date hereof, all of which are subject to change, possibly with retroactive effect. The discussion is not a full discussion of all tax considerations that may be relevant to the ownership and
</P>
 <p STYLE="margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt ; font-size:8pt">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center">14 </P>

disposition of ADSs or Class&nbsp;B shares and does not address the Medicare tax on net investment income or the effects of any state, local or foreign tax laws. The discussion applies only if
you will hold the ADSs and/or the Class&nbsp;B shares as capital assets and you use the USD as your functional currency. It does not deal with the tax treatment of investors subject to special rules, such as grantor trusts, real estate investment
trusts, regulated investment companies, banks, brokers or dealers in securities or currencies, traders in securities that elect to use a <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">mark-to-market</FONT></FONT> method of
recording for their securities holdings, financial institutions, insurance companies, persons required to accelerate the recognition of any item of gross income with respect to our ADSs or Class&nbsp;B shares as a result of such income being
recognized on an applicable financial statement, <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">tax-exempt</FONT> entities, investors liable for alternative minimum tax, holders (either actually or constructively) of 10% or more of the voting power or the value
of our shares, persons holding ADSs and/or Class&nbsp;B shares as part of a hedging, straddle, conversion or constructive sale transaction and persons who are resident or ordinarily resident in Sweden. In addition, investors holding ADSs and/or
Class&nbsp;B shares indirectly through partnerships are subject to special rules not discussed below. You should consult your own tax advisors about the United States federal, state, local and foreign tax consequences to you of the ownership and
disposition of the ADSs or Class&nbsp;B shares. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:9%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The discussion below applies to you only if you are a beneficial owner of ADSs and/or
Class&nbsp;B shares not resident in Sweden for purposes of the U.S. Tax Treaty and you are, for United States federal income tax purposes, (1)&nbsp;a citizen or resident of the United States, (2)&nbsp;a corporation or any other entity treated as a
corporation that is organized in or under the laws of the United States or its political subdivisions, including the District of Columbia, (3)&nbsp;a trust if all of the trust&#146;s substantial decisions are subject to the control of one or more
United States persons and the primary supervision of the trust is subject to a United States court, or if a valid election is in effect with respect to the trust to be taxed as a United States person, or (4)&nbsp;an estate the income of which is
subject to United States federal income taxation regardless of its source. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:9%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The discussion below assumes that the representations
contained in the deposit agreement governing the ADSs are true and that the obligations in the deposit agreement and any related agreement will be complied with in accordance with the terms. If you hold ADSs, you will be treated as the holder of the
underlying Class&nbsp;B shares represented by those ADSs for United States federal income tax purposes. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><U>Dividends </U></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:9%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Subject to the passive foreign investment company rules discussed below, the gross amount of dividends paid (before reduction for any Swedish
withholding taxes) with respect to the ADSs or Class&nbsp;B shares generally will be included in your gross income as ordinary income from foreign sources to the extent paid out of our current or accumulated earnings and profits (as determined for
United States federal income tax purposes). Distributions in excess of earnings and profits will be treated as a <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-taxable</FONT> return of capital to the extent of your adjusted tax basis in the ADSs or
Class&nbsp;B shares and thereafter as capital gain. The dividends will not be eligible for the dividends received deduction available to corporations in respect of dividends received from other U.S. corporations. The amount of any dividend paid in
SEK will be the USD value of the dividend payment based on the exchange rate in effect on the date of receipt (or constructive receipt) by you, in the case of Class&nbsp;B shares, or by the depositary, in the case of ADSs, whether or not the payment
is converted into USD at that time. Your tax basis in the SEK received will equal such USD amount. Gain or loss, if any, recognized on a subsequent sale or conversion of the SEK will be U.S. source ordinary income or loss. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:9%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">If you are a <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-corporate</FONT> holder of ADSs or Class&nbsp;B shares, dividends you receive on the ADSs or
Class&nbsp;B shares may be taxed at the lower applicable long-term capital gains rate provided that (1)&nbsp;we are not a passive foreign investment company (as discussed below) for either our taxable year in which the dividend was paid or the
preceding taxable year, (2)&nbsp;certain holding period requirements are met, (3)&nbsp;you are not under any obligation to make related payments with respect to substantially similar or related property and (4)&nbsp;either (a) in the case of ADSs
our ADSs continue to be listed on the Nasdaq Stock Market (or a national securities exchange that is registered under section 6 of the Securities Exchange Act of 1934, as amended) or (b)&nbsp;we are eligible for the benefits of the U.S. Tax Treaty.
You should consult your own tax advisors regarding the availability of the lower rate for dividends paid with respect to ADSs or Class&nbsp;B shares. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:9%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Subject to certain limitations, you will generally be entitled to receive credit against your United States federal income tax liability (or a
deduction against your United States federal taxable income) with respect to any Swedish tax withheld in accordance with the U.S. Tax Treaty and paid over to Sweden. If a refund of the tax withheld is available to you under the laws of Sweden or
under the U.S. Tax Treaty, the amount of tax withheld that is refundable will not be eligible for such credit against your United States federal income tax liability (and will not be eligible for the deduction in computing your United States federal
taxable income). For foreign tax credit limitation purposes, dividends will be income from sources without the United States, and will generally be treated as &#147;passive category income&#148; (or, in the case of certain holders, &#147;general
category income&#148;). </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><U>Sale or Exchange of ADSs or Class&nbsp;B shares </U></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:9%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Subject to the passive foreign investment company rules discussed below, you will generally recognize capital gain or loss on the sale or other
disposition of the ADSs or Class&nbsp;B shares equal to the difference between the USD value of the amount realized and your adjusted tax basis (determined in USD) in the ADSs or Class&nbsp;B shares. Such gain or loss will generally be long-term
capital gain or loss if you have held the ADSs or Class&nbsp;B shares for more than one year, and will generally be treated as arising from U.S. sources for foreign tax credit limitation purposes. If you are a
<FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-corporate</FONT> holder of ADSs or Class&nbsp;B Shares, long-term capital gains are eligible for reduced rates of taxation. The deductibility of capital losses is subject to limitations. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:9%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The amount realized on a disposition of ADSs or Class&nbsp;B shares for cash will generally be the amount of cash you receive for the ADSs or
Class&nbsp;B shares (which, in the case of payment in a <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-U.S.</FONT> currency, will equal the USD value of the payment received determined on (a)&nbsp;the date of receipt of payment if you are a cash basis
taxpayer and (b)&nbsp;the date of disposition if you are an accrual basis taxpayer). If the ADSs or Class&nbsp;B shares are treated as traded on an &#147;established securities market&#148; and you are a cash basis taxpayer (or, if you are an
accrual basis taxpayer, if you so elect), you will determine the USD value of the amount realized by translating the amount received at the spot rate of exchange on the settlement date of the sale. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:9%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">You will have a tax basis in any foreign currency received equal to the USD value thereof on the date of receipt. Any gain or loss you realize
on a subsequent sale or conversion of foreign currency will be U.S. source ordinary income or loss. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><U>Passive Foreign Investment Company Status </U></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:9%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">A <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-U.S.</FONT> corporation is a passive foreign investment company (a &#147;PFIC&#148;) in any taxable year
in which, after taking into account the income and assets of certain subsidiaries, either (a)&nbsp;at least 75% of its gross income is passive income or (b)&nbsp;at least 50% of the quarterly average value of its assets is attributable to assets
that produce or are held to produce passive income. Based on the market value of our shares, the composition of our assets and income and our operations, we believe we were not a PFIC during the year 2019. However, whether or not we will be
considered a PFIC will depend on the nature and source of our income and the composition and value of our assets, as determined from time to time. If we are treated as a PFIC, we will not provide information necessary for the &#147;qualified
electing fund&#148; election as the term is defined in the relevant provisions of the Code. You should consult your own tax advisors about the consequences of our potential classification as a PFIC. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:9%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">If we were classified as a PFIC with respect to your ADSs or Class&nbsp;B shares for any taxable year, we would generally continue to be a
PFIC (unless certain conditions are met), and you would be subject to special rules with respect to: </P> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
